+Jamison Brereton

107 (819)
Soma Pavama╠Дna
Seven Seers
26 verses: br╠еhat─л alternating with satobr╠еhat─л, arranged in prag─Бthas, except dvipad─Б vir─Бj bhurij 3 and dvipad─Б vir─Бj 16 as supplemental verses to the preceding prag─Бtha
This long hymn mostly stays focused the usual themes of the IXth Maс╣Зс╕Нala: the pressing of Soma, his journey across the filter, his entry into the waters, his mixing with cowsтАЩ milk, and his arrival at his destination, the wooden cups. Interspersed1354 IX.107
are references to SomaтАЩs cosmic aspect (e.g., the heavenly udder in vs. 5) and cos mic deeds (e.g., making the sun mount in heaven, vs. 7). Especially prominent in the middle and late parts of the hymn are mentions of the sea (vss. 9, 14, 15, 16, 21, 23), referring both to the waters that the soma enters and to the expanse of soma itself.
Toward the end the hymn takes a slightly personal turn, in the prag─Бtha of verses 19тАУ20, where the poet celebrates his fellowship with Soma and, by implication, the mental state he achieves from drinking the soma. In particular, 20cd тАЬWe have flown like birds far past the sun…тАЭ recalls several famous 1st-person descriptions of somaтАЩs effects: VIII.48.3 тАЬWe have drunk the soma; we have become immortal; we have gone to the light; we have found the godsтАЭ and X.119, the Laba-s┼лkta, in which the soma-drinker flies through the cosmos, describing his birdтАЩs eye view of heaven and earth.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬSprinkle from hence the effused Soma-juice which is the best oblation (to the gods), and which, good for man, is going into the midst of the firmament; (the priest) has expressed the Soma with the stones.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

From here sprinkle around the pressed drink, which is the soma, the highest oblation.
The manly one who has run within the waters, the soma did he [=the priest] press with stones.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The vs. begins with a most unusual sandhi: p├бr─лt├│ с╣гi├▒cat─Б. Geldner (n. 1a; cf. ZDMG 65: 307) suggests that it is Prakritizing. Oldenberg and Renou, less dramatically, consider it to be based on IX.63.10 p├бr─лto v─Бy├бve sut├бm, where the sandhi of it├бs is correct. (Geldner also cites this vs.) Renou points out that that vs. ends with si├▒cata and suggests that the unusual sandhi here тАЬr├йsulte de lтАЩassemblage des extr├йmit├йs du v.

63,10.тАЭ Although the invocation of 63.10 seems apposite, it doesnтАЩt entirely explain the sandhi we find here. The -o of p├бr─лt├│ can be explained as the adoption of this word sequence from its position before vd. C in 63.10, but the retroflexion in с╣гi├▒cat─Б does not follow. In fact, in 63.10, though si├▒cata occurs after -u (v─Б╠Бreс╣гu si├▒cata), there is no ruki-induced retroflexion over morpheme boundary (nor do we expect it).

Instead I think we must explain the retroflexion as an effect of the preverb p├бri. By far the greatest number of the retroflexed initials of this root occur immediately after p├бri, esp. the passive stem (pari) с╣гicy├б- (15 exx.), but also the ppl. p├бriс╣гikta- (8x); see also, in the next hymn (IX.108.7), our exact 2nd pl. act. impv. p├бri с╣гi├▒cata. There is also retroflexion after the preverb n├н (5+), and after the particles t┼л╠Б(2x) and h├н (1x). All of these are contact-induced, unlike our example, where the preverb is separated from the verb. Under these circumstances, there is ordinarily no retroflexion (see p├бri тАж si├▒cata X.32.5, p├бri тАж sikt├бс╕е IX.97.15). However, here I think either the numerous exx. of p├бri тИЪс╣гic in IX (15+) imposed distant retroflexion here where it was phonologically unmotivated, or an unretroflexed initial was changed redactionally under the influence of p├бri с╣гi├▒cata in the next hymn.

+Griffith

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬ(Soma) who are unassailable, who are most fragrant, flow around now being purified by the fleece; being effused we praise you eminent in the waters mixing you with food and the (products of the) kind.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

With food: andhs─Б = saktu, flour

+Jamison Brereton

Now, while being purified by the sheep, flow around as one who is undeceivable, very sweet-smelling.
Even when (you) have just been pressed in the waters, we become
exhilarated by your stalk, while preparing you with cows as the higher (oblation),

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The 2nd hemistich of this vs. is intricately interwoven with constituents overlapping; see OldenbergтАЩs sensible treatment at loc. The initial loc. expression consists of sut├й cit тАж aps├║, with tv─Б interspersed in modified 2nd position. This tv─Б is not to construed with the nearby verb mad─Бma (pace Grassmann), because m├бda- without preverb is almost never construed with an acc.; here that verb goes with the instr. ├бndhas─Б. The tv─Б finally finds its governing verb form in the participle ┼Ыr─лс╣З├бntaс╕е beginning p─Бda d; it is so distant from it, with parts of two different constituents in between, because it took WackernagelтАЩs position in the clause. The adj. ├║ttaram at the very end of the vs. modifies it: the soma is тАЬhigherтАЭ or тАЬbetterтАЭ at this point presumably because the mixing with milk, the last step depicted, improves it.

+Griffith

Now, being purified, flow hither through the fleece inviolate and most odorous.
We ladden thee in waters when thou art effused, blending thee still with juice and milk.

+Geldner

Dich l├дuternd flie├Яe jetzt durch die Schafhaare unbeirrt, bestduftend ab! Schon wenn er ins Wasser ausgepre├Яt ist, berauschen wir uns an dem Tranke, indem wir dich, den Trefflichsten, mit Kuhmilch mischen.

+Grassmann

Dich kl├дrend str├╢me durch des Widders Wolle nun, sch├╢nduftend, du untr├╝glicher; Gepresst auch laben dich mit Trank in Wassern wir, dich sch├╢nen mischend mit der Milch.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬBeing effused the Indu flows so as to be seen (of all)– the exhilarator of the gods, the agent (in holy acts), the observer of all.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Being pressed all around to be seenтАФthe exhilarator of the gods, the wide-gazing drop that is resolve.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Both Geldner and Renou make this vs. a separate cl., supplying a verb (тАЬfliesst,тАЭ тАЬcouleтАЭ), generated from p├бri srava in 2a, suggested by the init. p├бri in 3a. This is certainly possible, but since this vs. is an afterthought to the prag─Бtha, I take it as dependent on vs. 2, specifically 2ab, simply stringing together more descriptors of soma.

Note c├бkс╣гase тАж vicakс╣гaс╣З├бh.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬUndergoing purification you flow Soma in a stream clothed in the (consecrated) waters; the giver of wealth you sit on the plural ce of sacrifice, divine (Soma), who flow forth, who are the origin of gold.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Dev─Бn─Бm hitaramaс╣З─лyaс╕е = deva hiraс╣Зyayaс╕е

+Jamison Brereton

O Soma, you rush while being purified in a stream and clothing yourself in the waters.
Conferring treasure, you sit here upon the womb of truth as the golden wellspring, o god.

+Griffith

Cleansing thee, Soma, in thy stream, thou flowest in a watery robe:
Giver of wealth, thou sittest in the place of Law, O God, a fountain made of gold.

+Geldner

Gel├дutert flie├Яest du, Soma, in Str├╢men, dich in das Wasser h├╝llend. Du, der Lohnbringer, setzest dich auf den ordnungsgem├д├Яen Platz, du der goldene Born, o Gott.

+Grassmann

Geh├╝llt in Wasser fliessest du im Strom, o Soma, flammender, Und setzest spendend in den Schooss des Opfers dich, o Gott, als goldne Quelle du.

+Elizarenkova

The…celestial udder: i.e., the Soma

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬSoma flows forth the showerer of benefits, the best of path-finders, a с╣Ыс╣гi, a sage, all-discriminating; you are a seer, most devoted to the gods; you have made the sun to mount the sky.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Soma the rewarder purifies himself, the best pathfinder, the inspired, wide-gazing seer.
You became the sage poet who best pursues the gods. You made the sun mount in heaven.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The two splvs ending the a and c p─Бdas show a nice phonological relationship: (g─Бtu-)v├нt-tama- and (deva-)v─л╠Б-tama, with interchange between long vowel + single cons. and short vowel + geminate in otherwise identical phonetic seequences, an effect reminiscent of MIA quantitative trade-offs.

+Griffith

Bountiful, best of furtherers, Soma floweth on, Rsi and Singer, keen of sight.
Thou hast become a Sage most welcome to the Gods: thou madest Surya mount to heaven.

+Geldner

Soma, der Lohngeber, l├дutert sich, der beste Pfadfinder, der beredte, hellsehende Rishi. Du wardst der Seher, der am besten die G├╢tter einl├дdt. M├╢gest du die Sonne am Himmel aufsteigen lassen.

+Grassmann

Der Soma rieselt huldvoll, schaffend freiste Bahn, der weise S├дnger weiten Blicks, Du bist ein Seher, du der G├╢tter-labendste, die Sonn’ erhobst am Himmel du.

+Wilson

+Jamison Brereton

delighting stream.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Since ├б┼Ыvay─Б is fem., the tr. should be emended to тАЬwith a golden mare.тАЭ See GeldnerтАЩs disc. (n. 8cd) and dismissal of RothтАЩs proposed emendation (also rejected by Oldenberg), to bring out the comparison of the stream of soma to the urine stream of a horse, which, as Geldner points out, is still possible without emendation.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬSoma combined with the produce of the kine flows with the kine into the pitcher, he flows with the milked kine; his enjoyable juices go (to the pitcher as waters) to the ocean, the exhilarating (Soma) is expressed for the exhilaration (of the gods).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Into the pitcher: anupe = on the bank; or, in a watery low-lying plural ce, nimne de┼Ыe

+Jamison Brereton

Provided with cows he has flowed together with the cows at the waterтАЩs edge; Soma has flowed together with those that have been milked.
They have gone into the enclosures as if into the sea. The invigorating one wells out for exhilaration.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Both instances of akс╣г─Бс╕е should probably be read with distracted 2nd syllable, to provide the right no. of syllables in b and the right cadence in both p─Бdas.

In addition, p─Бda a is metrically deficient, even with this distracted reading. We expect a 12-syl. p─Бda in the Satobс╣Ыhat─л that provides the 2nd vss. of the prag─Бthas in this hymn; the Anukr. simply identifies the vs. instead as a Bс╣Ыhat─л, which should have an 8-syl. p─Бda in this position. Even without distracted akс╣г─Бс╕е, it would have 9 syllables, and with the distraction 10. Best to consider it a deficient Satobс╣Ыhat─л, which is the vs.-form expected, than an over-abundant Bс╣Ыhat─л. As for ways to make up the deficiency, see Oldenberg A distracted reading of an┼лp├й would provide at least one more syllable as well as a standard 4-syl. opening; however, neither etym. (*anu-Hp-├б-; see EWA s.v.) nor the other occurrence of the stem (X.27.23) favors this distraction.

Oldenberg rather exasperatedly suggests that the metrical disturbances in this vs. (see also the Triс╣гс╣нubh cadence of c in a 12-syl. p─Бda) may result from тАЬmangelhaftes Formgef├╝hl des Vfs.тАЭ

+Griffith

Down to the water-Soma, rich in kine hath flowed with cows, with cows that have been milked.
They have approached the mixing-vessel as a sea: the cheerer streams for the carouse.

+Geldner

Ein Kuhbesitzer im Marschland, mit seinen K├╝hen kam er geflossen, kam Soma mit den Gemolkenen geflossen. Sie sind in die Gehege gegangen wie die Fl├╝sse ins Meer. Der Berauschende ergie├Яt sich zum Rausche.

+Grassmann

Schon rann ins Becken mit der Milch der K├╝he Herr, Soma mit der gemolkenen; Die Tr├дnke, ihn umh├╝llend, liefen wie ins Meer, erfreuend trieft zum Rausche er.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬExpressed by the stones, Soma, (passing) through the sheep’s hairs, green-tinted, entering the cups as a man (enters) a city, you take your seat in the wooden (vessels).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

O Soma, while you are being pressed by the stones, (you come) here across the sheepтАЩs fleeces.
Like a man into a fortress, the tawny one enters into the two cups. You have established your seat in the woods [/in the wooden cups].

+Jamison Brereton Notes

With Geldner, Renou, Hoffmann (133), in the published translation I supply a verb in ab. I now think this may be unnec. The impetus was the apparent change of person between the first hemistich and the second: with voc. soma in p─Бda a but a 3rd ps. verb (vi┼Ыat) with Soma as subj. in c. However, as in vs. 12 the 3rd-ps. verb may result from attraction to the simile (j├бno n├б pur├н тАж vi┼Ыat тАЬas a man enters a fortressтАЭ), and the underlying person could be 2nd throughout; see dadhiс╣гe in d. It is hard to convey the change in Engl. but something like тАЬO Soma, while you are being pressed by the stones here across the sheep’s fleeces, as a man enters a fortress, as tawny one (you enter) into the two cups. You have established тАжтАЭ Hoffmann (133) argues that the changes of ps. mark p─Бda c as parenthetic, allowing it to be interpr. in his тАЬgeneralтАЭ sense. This sense should be possible even without branding the p─Бda as a parenthesis.

+Griffith

Effused by stones, O Soma, and urged through the long wool of the sheep,
Thou, entering the saucers as a man the fort, gold-hued hast settled in the wood.

+Geldner

Mit Steinen ausgepre├Яt l├дufst du, Soma, durch die Schafhaare ab. Der Falbe zieht in die beiden Camugef├д├Яe ein wie die Mannschaft in die Burg. Du hast deinen Sitz in den Holzgef├д├Яen genommen.

+Grassmann

Von Somasteinen ausgepresst geht Soma durch des Widders Haar, Der goldne ins Gef├дss wie in die Burg der Held; in Kufen nahmst du deinen Sitz.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬDesirous of (bestowing) food, passing through the interstices of the fleece the Soma is adorned like a horse in the battle; the Pavam─Бna, to be rejoiced in (by all, praised) by the intelligent, the sages, the reciters of sacred songs.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

He has become groomed across the fine (hairs) of the ewe, like a prize-seeking team at a competition.
Self-purifying Soma is to be cheered on by those of inspired thought, by the inspired reciters of verses.

+Griffith

He beautifies himself through the sheep’s long fine wool, like an impetuous steed in war,
Even Soma Pavamana who shall be the joy of sages and of holy bards.

+Geldner

Er wurde sauber gemacht, durch die feinen Haare des Schafs laufend wie ein um den Preis wettlaufendes Gespann, der Soma Pavamana, von den Sinnreichen zu bejubeln, von den beredten S├дngern.

+Grassmann

Er dringt gereinigt durch der Wolle Rinnen hin, ein Ross, das Preis im Kampf erstrebt; Der Soma, der von S├дngern hoch zu r├╝hmen ist, von jubelnden der flammende.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬYou are fed with water, Soma, like a river, for the banquet of the gods; with the juice of your filament you go to the honey-dropping receptacle, exhilarating, vigilant.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

O Soma, like a river that has swollen with its flood, you have swollen forth with the milk of the plant to pursue the gods,
wakeful like an exhilarating drink, toward the cask dripping
with honey.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich of this vs. is structured exactly like the more expansive 10a-c above: with a vocative soma in the 1st p─Бda and a following 3rd ps.

verb (pipye), which owes its 3rd ps. to attraction to the simile surrounding it, s├нndhur n├б тАж ├бrс╣Зas─Б. Geldner (n. 12b) explicitly attributes the 3rd ps. pipye to тАЬAttraktion an den Vergleich,тАЭ though he keeps the 2nd and 3rd ps. strictly separate in vs. 10. The 2nd ps. in the published translation, тАЬyou have swollen forth,тАЭ should, strictly speaking, be in parens.

Geldner and Renou make heavier weather of the 2nd hemistich than I think nec. or desirable. Because they strictly break the syntax at the end of b, they need to find something to do with the instr. phrase that opens c, aс╣Г┼Ы├│с╕е p├бyas─Б, which then leads them to interpr. j─Б╠Бgс╣Ыviс╕е as (unprecedentedly) transitive, which then leads them to supply an obj. for it - way too much machinery for something that can be far more simply interpr. The impetus for all this, the instr. phrase in c, can easily be taken as part of the simile/frame construction starting in b, with p├бyas─Б corresponding to ├бrс╣Зas─Б in the simile.

Now, as to their transitive j─Б╠Бgс╣Ыvi-. To be fair, it is not only the instr. phrase at the beginning of the p─Бda but also the apparent ineptness of the simile madir├│ n├б j─Б╠Бgс╣Ыviс╕е that lead them to their baroque interpr. The problem with the simile is that it seems to be a straight description of Soma, not a simile: the apparent meaning тАЬwakeful like an exhilarating drinkтАЭ or тАЬlike a wakeful exhilarating drinkтАЭ is a fine literal (or as literal as we get in the RV) characterization of soma. Both madir├б- and j─Б╠Бgс╣Ыvi- regularly modify Soma, the latter even in vs. 6 in this same hymn. As Geldner says (n. 12c), тАЬn├б als Vergleichswort macht Schwierigkeit.тАЭ And so both scholars search for ways to make this a real simile, which requires both words to be given senses they donтАЩt ordinarily have. They take madir├б- as referring to alcohol or some inebriating drink other than soma - even though it is never so used in the RV. And then, though j─Б╠Бgс╣Ыvi- only means тАШwakefulтАЩ in the RV as far as I can tell, including in vs. 6, they take it as expressing the effect that this other drink has on its drinkers: making wakeful, invigorating. And this all adds up to тАЬAvec le lait de ta tige, toi (qui rends lтАЩhomme) vif comme (fait lтАЩalcool) enivrant тАжтАЭ / тАЬMit der Milch des Stengels munter (machend) wie der berauschende (Branntwein) тАжтАЭ Although I realize that the simile is awkwardly comparing soma with a standard description of itself, the cure suggested by Geldner/Renou seems worse than the disease. I have several, not particularly satisfying suggestions for why we get a simile here. It may be that it is part of a simile chain: soma compared to a river, which in turn is compared to soma.

See VII.103.7ab (the frog hymn), where the frogs are compared to brahmins, who are in turn compared to frogs. Or else the animatized Soma the god is compared to soma the drink. But in any case, I prefer to accept the simile at face value, however clumsy, rather than erecting a fantastic superstructure by reinterpretating standard somic descriptors.

+Griffith

O Soma,-for the feast of Gods, river-like he hath swelled with surge,
With the stalk’s juice, exhilarating, resting not, into the vat that drops with meath.

+Geldner

Du Soma bist f├╝r die G├╢ttereinladung angeschwollen wie die Sindhu mit ihrer Flut. Mit der Milch des Stengels munter machend wie der berauschende Branntwein gehst du in die von S├╝├Яigkeit ├╝berflie├Яende Kufe.

+Grassmann

Gleich wie das Meer von Wogenflut schwoll Soma an zum G├╢ttermahl, Wie mit des Krautes Milch berauschend munter eilt zum Fass er, das von Honig trieft.

propelledтАФthe lofty truth,

+Jamison Brereton Notes

On Soma identified as тАЬtruthтАЭ (с╣Ыt├бm), see IX.97.23, IX.108.8, and L├╝ders 581-82. Although с╣Ыt├бс╣Г bс╣Ыh├бt could be an acc. goal here, the parallels, esp. the identical p─Бda in the next hymn, IX.108.8, support a nom. identification. In IX.97.23-24 Soma is also identified as a king (r─Б╠Бj─Б 24b) as here and as тАШpossessing dh├бrmanтАЩ (dharm─Б╠Б23c), reminiscent of dh├бrmaс╣З─Б here.

The Pp. analyses ├бrс╣гan opening c as injunc. ├бrс╣гat, while the published translation assumes a nom. sg. pres. part. ├бrс╣гan. Either is of course possible, but the parallelism with vs. initial t├бrat may support the finite verb interpr., as Oldenberg points out. So an alt. tr. would be: тАЬhe rushes тАжтАЭ See Hoffmann (117) on this vs.; he is surely right that the two injunctives should receive the same interpr., rather than RenouтАЩs indic. pres. t├бrat, modal ├бrс╣гat, and HoffmannтАЩs тАЬgeneralтАЭ pres. interpr. seems apt here for both.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬIn your friendship, Indu Soma, I have rejoiced day by day; many (r─Бkс╣гasas) assail me, tawny-coloured (Soma); overcome these who surround me.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

O Soma, I rejoice in your fellowship (with me) every day, o drop.
Many things, o brown one, get me downтАФway down. Go past these
barriers.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The indic. pf. of тИЪran is presential in value; see K├╝mmel (413). The form here echoes raс╣Зyati in 18b.

The lexeme n├н тИЪcar (or n├н ├бva тИЪcar) is found nowhere else in the RV or later.

The context clearly requires a negative sense; IтАЩve used the colloquial English idiom тАЬget (s.o.) down,тАЭ meaning тАШdiscourage, demoralizeтАЩ. There are two ways to interpr.

├бva at the end of the p─Бda. With Grassmann (and implicitly Geldner and Renou), I take it as a 2nd preverb with caranti. Since n├н and ├бva both mean тАШdownтАЩ, it reinforces by variation, hence my тАЬтАФway down.тАЭ As Geldner reports (n. 19c), Ludwig takes ├бva rather as the impv. to тИЪav тАШhelpтАЩ, accented because it starts a new clause. This is perfectly possible and would fit the context, but I prefer the more unusual semantic doubling of the preverbs in this emotional context.

There are various suggestions about what to supply with pur┼л╠Бс╣Зi: S─Бyaс╣Зa. r├бkс╣г─Бс╣Гsi, fld. tentatively by Geldner (тАЬb├╢se Geister?тАЭ), Renou тАЬchoses (dangereuses).тАЭ Leaving it open seems to me the better solution: the poet is besieged by multiple things he cannot even name.

In the last p─Бda it is Soma who is urged to тАЬgo past the barriersтАЭ (paridh─л╠Бn); we might have expected the poet to ask Soma for help in getting past them himself (but see next vs.). For SomaтАЩs journey past the paridh─л╠Бn Geldner and Renou cite IX.96.11 paridh─л╠Бm╠Рr ├бporс╣Зu тАЬopen up the barriers.тАЭ In both passages the paridh├н- are presumably obstacles to SomaтАЩs progress on his ritual journey, perhaps the tufts of the fleece filter.

+Griffith

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬI (delight) in your presence, tawny-coloured Soma, both day and night, for the sake of your friendship may we soar like birds far beyond the sun blazing with your light.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

S─Бmaveda has tav─Бham for ut─Бham; duhanaс╕е for sakhy─Бya; far beyond the sun: paraс╕е is an adjective for s┼лryam;

S┼лryam = soma, may we fly to you, the distant sun

+Jamison Brereton

Both by night and by day, Soma, I am at your udder for fellowship with you, o brown one.
We have flown like birds far past the sun that scorches with its heat.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is identical in conceptual structure to 19. The first hemistich expresses the 1st-ps. speakerтАЩs constant close relationship to Soma, using the word sakhy├б- тАШfellowshipтАЩ and an тАЬevery dayтАЭ expression (div├й-dive in 19b, n├бktam ut├б тАж div─Б╠Бin 20a). The 2nd iteration is more intimate than the first: in 19 the poet simply rejoices in his fellowship, but in 20 he is тАЬat your udder for fellowshipтАЭ (sakhy─Б╠Бya тАж ┼л╠Бdhani, suggesting a mother/child suckling relationship.

As for this ┼л╠Бdhani: because this occurrence is followed by the phrase ghс╣Ыс╣З─Б╠Б t├бpantam тАЬscorching with its heatтАЭ and because ┼л╠Бdhar / ┼л╠Бdhan- is found in V.34.3 in opposition to ghraс╣Гs├б- тАШheatтАЩ, Renou suggests that the two passages need to be interpr.

in conjunction with each other. For Renou this means rejecting the existence of an independent (┼л╠Бdhar /) ┼л╠Бdhan- meaning тАШcoldтАЩ (accepted by Geldner, EWA, and me), since тАШcoldтАЩ does not work in our passage. But I do subscribe to the two ┼л╠Бdhan- viewтАФsee comm. ad VIII.2.12тАФwith the one here belonging to the dominant тАШudderтАЩ stem. I simply consider the mention of scorching heat in the next hemistich to be coincidence.

The 2nd hemistich matches that of 19. In 19 the poet complains about his afflictions and then invites Soma to pass beyond the barriers. In this vs. the escape presumably effected by Soma in 19 provides the model for the one made by тАЬus.тАЭ Just as Soma was to go тАЬbeyond the barriersтАЭ (paridh─л╠Бс╣Гr ├бti) so did we fly (paptima) тАЬbeyond the sunтАЭ (├бti s┼л╠Бryam)тАФfar beyond it (p├бrah). The sun scorching with its heat, described in c, corresponds to the many things that got me down in 19c, and in both d p─Бdas these troubles are overcome, passed beyond. SomaтАЩs presumably successful journey beyond the barriersтАФbarriers that are probably ritually related (see above)тАФmakes it possible for us to overcome our own difficulties with triumphant flight.

Close to thy bosom am I, Soma, day and night. O Tawny-hued, for friendship sake.
Surya himself refulgent with his glow have we o’ertaken in his course like birds.

Und ich bin, o Soma, Nacht und Tag zur Freundschaft an deinem Euter, o Brauner. ├Ьber die hei├Я brennende Sonne hinaus sind wir gleich den gro├Яen V├╢geln geflogen.

+Grassmann

An deinem Euter, Soma, saug’ ich Tag und Nacht, zur Freundschaft, flammendrother du, Wie V├╢gel fliegen ├╝ber Sonnenglut wir fort, wenn sie uns sengt mit ihrem Strahl.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬFair-fingered (Soma) being cleansed you utter a sound in the pitcher; you bring, Pavam─Бna, ample golden-hued much-coveted wealth.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

While being groomed, dexterous one, you impel your speech upon the sea.
O self-purifying one, you rush toward ample, much-craved, golden
wealth.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Both Geldner and Renou construe samudr├й with mс╣Ыjy├бm─Бnaс╕е (e.g., тАЬIm Meer sauber gemachtтАЭ), but surely our passage can’t be separated from IX.12.6 pr├б v─Б╠Бcam ├нndur iс╣гyati, samudr├бsy─Б╠Бdhi viс╣гс╣н├бpi тАЬThe drop sends forth his speech upon the surface of the sea,тАЭ a passage adduced by Geldner (n. 21b) without comment.

+Geldner

+Griffith

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The injunc. v├н dh─Бrayaс╕е in c, in conjunction with pratham├бс╕е, invites a dual reading, both cosmogonic in the past and the ritual present. Hoffmann doesnтАЩt cite this passage.

+Griffith

тАЬYour purified juices are let flow through the filter in a stream accompanied by the Maruts, exhilarating plural asing Indra, swift-moving, bringing praise and food.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Swift-moving: hayaс╕е = horses, gant─Бraс╕е

+Jamison Brereton

Purifying themselves, they have been set loose across the filter in a steamтАФ
the exhilarating coursers, fit for Indra along with the Maruts, toward wisdom [/the ritual meal] and pleasing offerings.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda c is a clever twist on 17ab ├нndr─Бya тАж mar├║tvate sut├бс╕е тАЬpressed for Indra and the Maruts.тАЭ In 17 the recipients of the soma are straightforwardly expressed, but in our vs. the expression is oblique. Indra is present not directly, but in the adj. indriy├б- тАШIndriyan, suitable for/associated with Indra (and IndraтАЩs powers)тАЩ, which modifies the soma drops identified as horses. The adj. mar├║tvantaс╕е also modifies these drops/horses. On the one hand, I think this is meant to associate the Maruts with Indra, as usual, and identify them as the prototypical recipients of soma; on the other hand, however, the drop-horses are metaphorically associated with the Maruts in full gallop on their regularly described journeys. The double sense would be better conveyed by a transl. тАЬthe exhilarating courses, accompanied by the Maruts, fit for Indra along with the Maruts тАжтАЭ The fem. stem medh─Б╠Б- of course means тАШwisdomтАЩ and is so interpr. here by everyone (incl. me). But its explicit coordination with pr├бy─Бс╣Гsi тАЬpleasing offeringsтАЩ (medh─Б╠Бm abh├н pr├бy─Бс╣Гsi ca) invites, to my mind, a secondary reading associating it with m├йdha- тАШritual offering/mealтАЩ. For other possible conflations of medh─Б╠Б- and m├йdha- see EWA s.v. m├йdha-.

+Griffith

Over the cleansing sieve have flowed the Pavamanas in a stream,
Girt by the Maruts, gladdening, Steeds with Indra’s stiength, for wisdom and for dainty food.

+Geldner

Sich l├дuternd sind sie im Strome durch die Seihe gesprengt, von den Marut begleitet, berauschend, die indrischen Rosse, um Erkenntnis und Erquickung zu bringen.

+Grassmann

Ergossen sind die flammenden im Strome durch das Somasieb, Die lust’gen Rosse Indra’s und der Marutschar zum Opfer und zum Labetrunk.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬIndu clothed with waters effused by the worshippers rushes to the receptacle, genitive rating light, identifying its form with the (products of the) kine, he covets now (our) praises.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Clothing himself in the waters, he rushes around the cask, the drop being propelled by the pressers.
Begetting the light, he has made the delighting cows bellow, making the cows as if into his fresh garment.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

ap├│ v├бs─Бnaс╕е returns from 4b, 18c, along with the verb ├бrс╣гa-, ubiquitous in this hymn.

g─Б╠Бс╕е тАШcowsтАЩ needs to be read with both c and d. In the former it is the referent of the hapax mand├бn─Бс╕е (whose sense is, however, easy to divine) and the obj. of the caus. redupl. aor. тАШcauses to bellowтАЩ; in the latter it is the obj. of kс╣Ыс╣Зv─Бn├бс╕е and the target of the simile: тАЬmaking the cows as if into his garmentтАЭ (a simile that of course depends on a metaphor: cows = milk). I consider the n├б to be displaced - we might expect *nirс╣З├нjaс╣Г n├б. This p─Бda, in this order, is also found in IX.14.5; for variants on the phrase without simile particle see IX.86.26, 95.1, all adduced by Geldner (n. 26d).

+Griffith

Urged onward by the pressers, clad in watery robes, Indu is speeding to the vat.
He gendering light, hath made the glad Cows low, while he takes them as his garb of state.

+Geldner

In Wasser sich h├╝llend umflie├Яt er die Kufe, der von den Pressenden zur Eile getriebene Saft. Licht hervorbringend hat er die Jubellieder lautbar gemacht, indem er die Kuhmilch gleichsam zu seinem Festgewand macht.

+Grassmann

In Flut gekleidet str├╢mt er zu dem Fass hindurch von Pressern Indu ausgesandt, Licht zeugend schreit die K├╝h’ er an, die ihn erfreun, die Milch anlegend wie ein Kleid.

+Elizarenkova
